Husband's Right to Prevent Wife's Relatives: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on husband's authority over wife's visitors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi positions on a husband's authority over his wife's visitors and state the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling with its justification.

Core Idea
A husband can limit visits but not sever family ties—balance between property rights and kinship obligations.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explores a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: how much control does a husband have over who enters his home to visit his wife? While the house is his property, Islam strongly emphasizes maintaining family ties. The commentator presents three views and declares one as correct. Understanding this dispute teaches us how Hanafi scholars weigh competing principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling categories
What specific actions are under discussion? Identify: preventing entry, preventing seeing/speaking, preventing staying (prolonged visits), and preventing the wife from going out.
The act is the husband's exercise of authority over his home and wife's visitors.
2
Locate the three positions
Distinguish the first view (matn): husband can prevent entry but not seeing/speaking. Second view (qil): he can only prevent prolonged stays due to fitna. Third view (qil): he can prevent wife from going out but cannot prevent parents from entering every Friday.
The third is declared sahih (correct).
3
Determine the dalil for each position
First view: property rights (mulk). Second view: fitna from lingering. Third view: balancing property with prohibition of severing kinship (qati' rahim).
Note the role of qati' rahim as a stronger principle.
4
Identify the tarjih mechanism
The commentator prefers the third view because it avoids severing kinship (haram) while preserving the husband's authority to limit frequency.
The tarjih is based on preventing harm (daf' al-darar) and preserving both rights.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
State the operative ruling: husband can prevent wife from going out to parents but must allow them entry at least weekly; other mahram are analogized (qiyas).
This applies in modern contexts: husband cannot ban visits entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وله ان يمنع والديها وولدها من غيره واهلها من الدخول عليها لان المنزل ملكه فله حق المنع من دخول ملکه ولا يمنعهم من النظر اليها و کلامهافی ای وقت اختارو المافيه من قطيعة الرحم وليس له فى ذالك ضرر وقيل لا يمنع من الدخول والكلام و انما يمنعهم من القرار لان الفتنة فى اللباث وتطويل الكلام وقيل يمنعها من الخروج الى الوالدين ولا يمنعهما من الدخول عليها في كل جمعة وفي غيرهما من المحارم التقدير بسنته و هو الصحيح ترجمہ اور شوہر کو اختیار ہے کہ بیوی کے والدین کو اور اس کے لڑکے کو جو پہلے شوہر سے ہے اور اس کے گھر والوں کو اس کے پاس آنے سے روکے کیونکہ مکان اس کی ملک ہے، تو اسے اپنی ملک میں داخل ہونے سے روکنے کا حق ہے۔ اور وہ ان کو اس کے دیکھنے اور اس سے بات کرنے سے نہیں روک سکتا جب بھی وہ چاہیں، کیونکہ اس میں قطع رحمی ہے، اور اس میں اسے کوئی ضرر نہیں۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ وہ ان کو داخل ہونے اور بات کرنے سے نہیں روک سکتا، بلکہ وہ ان کو ٹھہرنے (قرار) سے روک سکتا ہے، کیونکہ فتنہ بیٹھنے اور لمبی بات کرنے میں ہے۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ وہ عورت کو والدین کے پاس جانے سے روک سکتا ہے، اور وہ ان کو ہر جمعہ میں اس کے پاس آنے سے نہیں روک سکتا۔ اور دوسرے محارم کا اندازہ اسی پر ہے، اور یہی صحیح ہے۔
And he has the right to prevent her parents and her son from other (husband) and her family from entering upon her, because the house is his property, so he has the right to prevent entry into his property. And he does not prevent them from looking at her and speaking to her at any time they choose, because in that there is severance of kinship, and there is no harm to him in that. And it is said: He does not prevent them from entering and speaking, rather he prevents them from staying (settling), because the fitna is in lingering and prolonging conversation. And it is said: He prevents her from going out to her parents, and he does not prevent them from entering upon her every Friday, and for other mahram the estimation is based on that, and this is the correct view.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage addresses the husband's authority in his home regarding the wife's relatives. The primary ruling (from the matn) is: The husband may prevent the wife's parents, her children from a previous marriage, and other relatives from entering the house because it is his property. However, he cannot prevent them from seeing or speaking to the wife, as that would sever family ties and does not harm him. Then the commentary (sharh) presents two other opinions (qil). The first says the husband cannot prevent entry and conversation at all; he can only prevent them from staying overnight or prolonged visits. The second opinion says the husband can prevent the wife from going out to her parents, but he cannot prevent them from visiting her every Friday, and other mahram are analogized to this. The commentator declares the last view as sahih (correct). This is a classic intra-Hanafi dispute with tarjih.

Key Terms
محارم (mahārim): Close male relatives with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as father, brother, etc.
قطع رحم (qati' rahim): Severing family ties, which is a sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct (sahih) view regarding the husband's right to restrict his wife's parents from visiting, according to this passage?
A) He can prevent them from entering and speaking entirely
B) He can prevent them from staying but not from entering and speaking
C) He can prevent the wife from going out to them, but cannot prevent them from entering every Friday
D) He cannot prevent them at all

Key Takeaway
A husband's property rights over his home are balanced by the obligation to preserve family ties, allowing regular mahram visits while preventing prolonged stays.

The Obligation of Exclusive Residence for the Wife
Explains that residence is wajib like nafaqah and husband cannot force sharing with son from another wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence for the obligation of residence (sukna) in Hanafi fiqh and apply the ruling to scenarios involving shared housing and sufficiency of a separate room.

Core Idea
The wife's right to exclusive residence is a wajib right proven by the Quranic imperative; the husband cannot force her to live with others.

In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah establishes that residence (sukna) is a distinct wajib obligation upon the husband, separate from nafaqah. He draws on the Quranic command 'askunuhunna' (Lodge them) as direct proof, refutes the notion that it is merely conjoined with nafaqah, and then examines the consequences of this right: the husband cannot share the home with his son from another wife without the wife's consent. Finally, he clarifies that providing a separate lockable room suffices when a fully independent house is not available.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is providing residence (sukna) for the wife. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) upon the husband, akin to nafaqah.
Note that the Hanafi school treats sukna as a separate wajib, not merely a part of nafaqah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse 'askunuhunna' (Surah Talaq 65:6) as the primary proof. Also references the maxim of harm (darar).
Also uses the principle that conjunction in wording does not imply conjunction in ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form 'askunuhunna' indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul. The harm that befalls the wife if others are present provides additional rationale.
Three specific harms are mentioned: insecurity, inhibition, and hindrance to intimacy.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools consider residence a part of nafaqah, not a separate wajib. The author argues against this by stating that the conjunction in wording does not establish conjunction in ruling.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within fiqh.
5
Apply the ruling to subsidiary cases
The passage then addresses two sub-rulings: (1) The husband cannot force the wife to live with his son from another wife unless she consents; (2) Providing a separate lockable room suffices as exclusive residence.
The wife's consent waives her right; the key is achieving the purpose of privacy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفقہ کی طرح سکتی بھی شوہر پر واجب ہے۔ یہاں صاحب ہدایہ نے جوفر مایا او جبہ اللہ مقرونا بالنفقة اس کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں تھی اس لئے کہ قران فی الظلم قران فی الکام پر دلالت نہیں کرتا۔ دوم یہ کہ سکونت کے وجوب کو ثابت کرنے کے ملئے باری تعالیٰ کا قول اسکنو هن کافی تھا۔ کیونکہ یہ صیغہ امر ہے اور امر کا صیغہ وجوب پر دلالت کرتا ہے بہر حال جب سکونت عورت کے واسطے حق واجبی ہوئی۔ تو مرد کے لئے جائز نہیں کہ اس کے حق میں غیر کو شریک کرے۔ کیونکہ عورت کو اس سے ضرر ہوتا ہے ایک تو اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے سامان سے بے خوف نہ ہوگی ۔ دوسرے یہ کہ غیر کی شرم سے شوہر کے ساتھ بے تکلف نہیں رہ سکتی اور تیسرے یہ کہ جماع اور متعلقات جماع سے روک ہوگی ۔ لیکن اگر عورت خود ہی اس بات پر راضی ہو کہ سسرال والوں کے ساتھ رہے تو یہ اس کے لئے جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے حق کی کمی پر خود راضی ہوئی۔ یعنی شوہر کے گھر والوں کو اس کے ساتھ رہنے سے اس کے حق کی وجہ سے منع کیا گیا تھا مگر جب اس نے خود اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا تو اس کے لئے کلام کی گنجائش نہیں ہوگی ۔
شوہر کا بیٹا اس کے علاوہ بیوی سے ہوشو ہرا سے اس مکان میں نہیں رکھ سکتا
و ان كان له ولدمن غيرها فليس له ان يسكنه معها لما بينا و لو اسكنها فى بيت من الدار مفر دوله غلق كفاها لان المقصود قد حصل
ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر کا لڑکا اس کے علاوہ دوسری بیوی سے ہو، تو شوہر کو اختیار نہیں کہ لڑکے کو اس کے ساتھ بساد تے ۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے اور اگر عورت کو شوہر نے گھر کے ایک تنہا کمرے میں جس کا بند کرنے کا دروازہ موجود ہو آباد کیا تو اس عورت کے واسطے کافی ہے۔ کیونکہ مقصود حاصل ہو گیا۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں دو مسئلے زیر بحث ہیں اول یہ کہ اگر شوہر کا لڑکا پہلی بیوی سے ہو تو شوہر کے لئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ لڑکے کو اس بیوی کے ساتھ آباد کرے۔ اس کی دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی کہ عورت کو ضرر ہوگا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے عورت کو گھر کے ایک تنہا کمرے میں جس کا بند کرنے کا دروازہ موجود ہے آباد کیا تو عورت کیلئے کافی ہے۔ کیونکہ مقصود حاصل ہو گیا۔ یعنی بغیر کراہت کے اس کے ساتھ جماع کرناممکن ہے۔
Just as [the obligation of] nafaqah, residence is also wajib on the husband. Here, the author of al-Hidayah said, 'And He obligated it, conjoined with nafaqah' – there is no need for this, because the conjunction in wording does not indicate conjunction in ruling. Secondly, to establish the obligation of residence, the saying of Allah Most High 'askunuhunna' (Lodge them) was sufficient, because this is an imperative form, and the imperative form indicates obligation. In any case, when residence became a wajib right for the woman, it is not permissible for the man to share [the house] with another in her right, because harm (darar) befalls the woman: first, she will not be safe with her belongings; second, due to the shame of the others, she cannot be free with her husband; third, she will be prevented from sexual intercourse and its preliminaries. However, if the woman herself agrees to live with the in-laws, it is permissible for her, because she consented to a reduction of her right. That is, the husband's household was prevented from living with her due to her right, but when she waived her right, there is no room for objection.

Then the Arabic text: 'And if he has a son from other than her, he has no right to lodge him with her, for what we have explained. And if he settles her in a room of the house that has a lockable door, it suffices her, because the purpose is achieved.'
Translation: And if the husband has a son from another wife, the husband has no authority to settle the son with her, due to the reason we explained. And if the husband settled the woman in a solitary room of the house that has a lockable door, it is sufficient for the woman, because the purpose is achieved.
Explanation: Two issues are discussed in this passage: First, if the husband's son is from the first wife, it is not permissible for the husband to settle the son with this wife, its proof has passed, that harm would befall the woman. Second, if the husband settles the woman in a solitary room of the house that has a lockable door, it is sufficient for the woman, because the purpose is achieved, i.e., it is possible to have intercourse with her without dislike.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and the principle of harm (darar). It establishes that residence (sukna) is a wajib right of the wife, separate from nafaqah. The author first argues that the Quranic imperative 'askunuhunna' directly establishes obligation, contrary to the idea that it is only conjoined with nafaqah. Then, he explains the ruling that the husband cannot force his wife to live with his son from another wife because it causes harm: loss of security, inhibition, and hindrance to intimacy. However, if the wife willingly agrees, it is valid because she is waiving her right. The Arabic matn adds that if the husband provides a separate room with a lockable door, it fulfills the purpose of privacy and the wife cannot demand further separation. This is a clear application of the principle that the wife's right is to exclusive lodging that prevents interference.

Key Terms
سکونت (sukna): Residence: the husband's obligation to provide a separate dwelling for the wife as her exclusive right.
وجوب (wujub): Legal obligation; a category between fard and sunnah in Hanafi fiqh.
ضرر (darar): Harm: the basis for prohibiting the husband from sharing the residence with others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It suffices for her because the purpose of privacy is achieved.
C) It is only valid if she agrees.
D) The husband must provide a separate building entirely.

Key Takeaway
Residence (sukna) is a distinct wajib right of the wife, proven by the Quranic imperative, and the husband cannot force her to share the home without her consent; a lockable room suffices.

Husband's Right to Prevent Relatives' Visits: Balancing Property and Kinship
Intra-Hanafi dispute on husband's right to prevent relatives' visits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a husband preventing mahram relatives from visiting his wife, explain the evidence, and apply the mufta bihi position regarding visit frequency.

Core Idea
The husband cannot prevent mahram relatives from seeing and speaking to his wife, but may limit stays to prevent fitna.

In this passage, we examine a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: while the husband owns the home and may bar entry, he cannot cut kinship ties by preventing mahram relatives from seeing and speaking to his wife. The text reconciles property rights with the duty to maintain family bonds, settling on specific visitation rights for parents (weekly) and other mahrams (yearly).

Guided Path
1
Identify the husband's general right
The husband can prevent anyone from entering his house because it is his property. Note the basis: 'al-manzilu milkuhu'.
2
Recognize the limit: mahram relatives
He cannot prevent them from seeing and speaking, as that would sever kinship (qati' al-rahim), which is haram based on the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im.
3
Understand the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Different views exist: some say he can only prevent staying, others say he can prevent her from going out but must allow entry, etc. The text weighs these.
4
Apply the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view: parents may visit once a week; other mahrams once a year. This balances property rights and kinship duties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر عورت کے ماں باپ، پہلے شوہر کے بیٹے کو اس کے پاس آنے سے روک سکتا ہے
وله ان يمنع والديها وولدها من غيره واهلها من الدخول عليها لان المنزل ملكه فله حق المنع من دخول ملکه ولا يمنعهم من النظر اليها و کلامهافی ای وقت اختارو المافيه من قطيعة الرحم وليس له فى ذالك ضرر وقيل لا يمنع من الدخول والكلام و انما يمنعهم من القرار لان الفتنة فى اللباث وتطويل الكلام وقيل يمنعها من الخروج الى الوالدين ولا يمنعهما من الدخول عليها في كل جمعة وفي غيرهما من المحارم التقدير بسنته و هو الصحيح
ترجمہ اور شوہر کو اختیار ہے کہ بیوی کے والدین کو اور اس کے لڑکے کو جو پہلے شوہر سے ہے اور اس کے گھر والوں کو اس کے پاس آنے

باب النفقة

سے رو کے کیونکہ یہ گھر تو شوہر کی ملک ہے تو اس کو اپنی ملک میں آنے سے منع کرنے کا اختیار حاصل ہے اور بیوی کے والدین وغیہ وکو جب کبھی وہ چاہیں اس عورت کی طرف دیکھنے اور اس کے ساتھ باتیں کرنے سے منع نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس میں قطع رقم ہے اور شوہر کے حق میں کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے اور کہا گیا کہ آنے اور باتیں کرنے سے منع نہ کرے۔ البتہ شہر نے سے منع کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ فساد مظہر نے اور بہت دیر جیک باتیں کرنے میں ہے اور کہا گیا کہ عورت کو والدین کے پاس جانے اور اس کے پاس آنے سے ہر جمعہ میں (ایک بار) منع نہیں کر سکتا اور والدین کے ملا وہ دوسرے محارم کے ( حق ) میں اندازہ ایک سال ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے
تشریح مسئلہ الشوہر کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ اپنی بیوی کے پاس اس کے ماں باپ اور اس کا لڑکا جو پہلے شوہرت ہے اس کو اور دوسرے رشتہ داروں کو آنے سے روکے دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ کھر تو شوہر کی ذاتی ملک ہے لہذا اس کو اپنی ملک میں آنے سے منع کرنے کا اختیار حاصل ہے اور اگر بیوی کے والدین وغیر ہ اس کو دیکھنا چاہتیں یا با تیں کرنا چاہیں تو ش ہر اس عورت کی طرف دیکھنے اور باتیں کرنے سے منع نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ اس میں قطع رحم لازم آتا ہے اور قطع رقم حرام ہے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے عن جبیر بن مطعم انه سمع التي يقول لا يدخل الجنة قاطع - يعنی جبیر بن مطعم سے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے حضور اقدس صلى الله عليه وسلم کو فرماتے ہوئے سنا کہ قطع رحم کرنے والا جنت سے تو میں داخل نہیں ہوگا اور عورت کی طرف ان کے دیکھنے اور باتیں کرنے سے شوہر کے حق میں کوئی ضر نہیں ہے اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ باتیں کرنے کی طرح ان کو آنے سے بھی منع نہیں کر سکتا۔ البتہ ٹھہرنے سے منع کر کتاب کیوں کہ فتنہ وفساداگر پیدا ہوا تو یہاں کلمہ نے اور بہت باتیں کرنے سے ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ زیادہ باتیں کرنا قیل وقال کا سبب ہوگا اور اس کا نتیجہ شر وفساد ہوگا۔ اور اکثر علماء نے کہا کہ عورت کو اپنے والدین کے یہاں جانے اور اس کے والدین کو یہاں آنے سے ہر جمعہ میں ایک بازی نہیں مریم ہے۔ بلکہ ہفتہ میں ایک بار ملاقات کرنے کی اجازت ہو گی۔ اسی پر فتویٰ ہے۔
اور والدین کے علاوہ دوسرے قرابت داروں کو سال میں ایک دفعہ ملاقات کرنے کی اجازت ہے خواہ عورت ان کے پاس جائے یا وہ یہاں آویں صحیح قول یہی ہے۔ بعض حضرات ایک ماہ میں ایک بار زیادہ کی اجازت دیتے ہیں۔
The husband can prevent the woman's parents, her son from the previous husband, and her relatives from coming to her. And he has the right to prevent her parents, her son from other than him, and her relatives from entering upon her because the house is his property, so he has the right to prevent entry into his property. And he does not prevent them from looking at her and speaking to her at any time they choose, because there is severance of kinship in that, and he has no harm in that. And it was said: he does not prevent them from entering and speaking, rather he prevents them from staying, because fitna is in staying and prolonged conversation. And it was said: he prevents her from going out to her parents, and does not prevent them from entering upon her every Friday; and other than them from mahrams, the estimate is once a year, and that is correct.

Translation: And the husband has the authority to prevent the wife's parents, and her son from the previous husband, and her relatives from coming to her. Because this house is the husband's property, so he has the right to prevent entry into his property. And the wife's parents etc., whenever they wish to look at this woman and speak with her, he cannot prevent, because in that is severance of kinship, and there is no harm to the husband. And it was said: he cannot prevent them from entering and speaking; rather, he can prevent them from staying, because the manifestation of discord is in staying and very long conversations. And it was said: the woman going to her parents and them coming to her once every Friday cannot be prevented; and other than parents from other mahrams, the estimate is one year, and this is correct.

Explanation: Issue: The husband has the authority to prevent the wife's parents, her son from the previous husband, and other relatives from coming to her. The proof is that this house is the husband's personal property, therefore he has the authority to prevent entry into his property. And if the wife's parents etc. want to see her or speak, the husband cannot prevent them from looking at the woman and speaking, because in that is severance of kinship, and severance of kinship is haram. For it is narrated from Jubayr ibn Mut'im that he heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: 'The one who severs kinship ties will not enter Paradise.' And there is no harm to the husband in them seeing and speaking to the woman. And some mashayikh said: just as he cannot prevent them from speaking, he cannot prevent them from entering; rather, he can prevent them from staying, because if fitna and corruption occur, it will be from staying and excessive talking. For excessive talking causes 'qila wa qal' and its result is evil and corruption. And most scholars said: the woman going to her parents and her parents coming here once every Friday cannot be prevented; rather, once a week meeting is permitted. This is the fatwa. And other than parents, other relatives are permitted to meet once a year, whether the woman goes to them or they come here. This is the correct saying. Some allow once a month more frequently.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the husband's right to prevent relatives from visiting his wife. The core ruling is that the husband, as owner of the house, can prevent entry. However, he cannot prevent them from seeing or speaking to the wife at any time because that would cut family ties, which is haram based on a hadith. There are different opinions within the madhhab: some say he can only prevent staying (not entry and speech), others say he can prevent her from going out to parents but must allow them to visit once a week, and for other mahrams once a year. The text declares the opinion of weekly visits for parents and yearly for other mahrams as correct (sahih) and the basis for fatwa. This shows the Hanafi school balancing the husband's property rights with the wife's right to maintain family relations.

Key Terms
قطع رحم (qati' al-rahim): Severing family ties; a major sin that the husband must avoid.
محارم (mahram): Permanent unmarriageable kin (e.g., parents, children, siblings).
فتنہ (fitna): Moral temptation or discord that may arise from prolonged visits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion in this text, how often can the wife's parents visit her?
A) Whenever they want without restriction.
B) Once every Friday (weekly).
C) Once a year.
D) Only if the husband agrees.

Key Takeaway
The husband must allow mahram relatives periodic visits to avoid severing family ties, with weekly for parents and yearly for other mahrams.

Assigning Nafaqah from Absent Husband's Money
Explains how a judge can assign nafaqah from money held by a third party who acknowledges the marriage and deposit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge can assign nafaqah from the absent husband's money held by a third party, and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A judge can assign nafaqah from an absent husband's money held by a person who acknowledges both the marriage and the deposit.

When a husband is absent and his money is in the possession of another person, the wife and dependents may be left without support. The Hanafi school allows the judge to assign nafaqah directly from that money if the holder acknowledges both the deposit and the marriage. This ruling balances the wife's right to maintenance with procedural fairness, relying on the legal effect of acknowledgment (iqrar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge assigning nafaqah from the absent husband's money held by a third party. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) for the judge to do so when conditions are met.
The ruling is based on the wife's established right to maintenance.
2
Locate the conditions for the ruling
Two conditions must be met: (1) The holder acknowledges both the deposit and the marriage, or the judge knows the facts independently. (2) The money held must be of the same type as the wife's right (e.g., dirhams, dinars, food, or clothing of similar kind).
If the money is of a different type, nafaqah cannot be assigned because conversion (sarf) would be needed, which is not the judge's role.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (dalil)
The proof is rational: the wife has the right to take her maintenance from her husband's wealth without his consent. The holder's acknowledgment is binding on himself regarding the deposit and marriage, and this acknowledgment transmits to the absent husband because the wife's right is established.
The holder's iqrar is accepted in his own right; if he denied either, the woman's evidence would not be sufficient against him.
4
Note the limits and exceptions
The ruling applies only when the money is the same type as her right. If it is of a different type, the judge cannot assign nafaqah directly. The same rule applies if the money is held as mudarabah or as a debt.
This ensures the assignment is straightforward without complex transactions.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
For example, if a husband travels abroad and his brother holds cash (same currency) and acknowledges the marriage, the judge can order maintenance from that cash for the wife and children.
The principle remains valid today for similar cases of absent husbands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر غائب ہو گیا اس کا مال ایک آدمی کے پاس تھا جو اس کا اقرار کرتا ہے کہ یہ عورت اس کی بیوی ہے تو قاضی مال میں غائب کی بیوی اور اولادصغار والدین کا نفقہ مقرر کر دے
و اذا غاب الرجل وله مال فى يدرجل يعترف به وبالزوجية فرض القاضي في ذالك المال نفقة زوجة الغائب و ولده الصغارو والديه وكذا اذا علم القاضى ذالك ولم يعترف به لانه لما اقربا لزوجية والوديعة فقد اقران حق الا خذلها لان لها ان تاخذ من مال الزوج حقها من غير رضاه و اقرار صاحب اليد مقبول في حق نفسه لاسيما ههنا فانه لو انكر احدا لامرين لاتقبل بيئة المرأة فيه لان المودع ليس بخصم في اثبات الزوجية عليه ولا المرأة خصم فى اثبات حقوق الغائب فاذا ثبت فى حقه تعدى الى الغائب وكذا اذا كان المال فى يده مضاربة وكذا الجواب في الدين وهذا كله اذاكان المال من جنس حقها دراهم او دنانير او طعاما او كسوة من جنس حقها اما اذا كان من خلاف جنسه لا تفرض النفقة فيه لانه يحتاج الى
The husband became absent, his money was with a man who acknowledges that this woman is his wife, then the judge in that money assigns nafaqah for the absent husband's wife, young children, and parents.

Arabic: And when a man is absent and he has money in the hand of a man who acknowledges the money and the marriage, the judge in that money assigns nafaqah of the absent husband's wife, his young children, and his parents. And likewise when the judge knows that and he (the holder) does not acknowledge it. Because when they both acknowledged the marriage and the deposit, they acknowledged the right of taking for her, for she has the right to take her right from the husband's money without his consent. And the acknowledgment of the person in possession is accepted regarding himself, especially here. For if he denied either of the two matters, the woman's evidence would not be accepted in it, because the depositor is not a party to establish the marriage against him, nor is the woman a party to establish the rights of the absent. So when it is established regarding him, it transmits to the absent. And likewise if the money is in his hand as mudarabah, and likewise the answer in debt. And all this when the money is of the same kind as her right: dirhams, dinars, or food, or clothing of the same kind as her right. But if it is of a different kind, nafaqah is not assigned in it, because it needs (to be converted).
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on the procedure for assigning nafaqah when the husband is absent and his money is held by someone who acknowledges both the deposit and the marriage. The key point is that the person in possession (the depositee) is not a stranger; his acknowledgment is binding on himself and transfers to the absent husband because the wife has the right to take her due. The judge can also act if he knows the facts even without acknowledgment. The ruling applies only if the money is of the same type as the wife's due (e.g., cash, food, clothing); if different, the judge cannot assign it directly because conversion (sarf) would be needed, which is not the judge's job. This shows the Hanafi concern for practical justice within legal procedures.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): A husband who is absent and whose whereabouts are unknown or he is in a distant place.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment; legal admission that binds the declarant.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance: food, clothing, and lodging for the wife and dependents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can the judge assign nafaqah from money held by a person who acknowledges the deposit but denies the marriage?
A) Yes, because the judge knows the truth.
B) No, because the woman's evidence is not accepted against the depositee regarding marriage.
C) Yes, if the woman provides two witnesses.
D) No, the judge must wait for the husband's return.

Key Takeaway
A judge can assign nafaqah from an absent husband's money held by a third party if the third party acknowledges both the deposit and the marriage, provided the money is of the same type as the wife's due.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate

Husband's Right to Prevent Entry but Not Visits
Explanation of husband's authority and its limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a husband's right to prevent his wife's relatives from entering his house, and distinguish between permissible prevention (entry, overnight stay) and prohibited prevention (seeing, speaking) with the underlying legal basis.

Core Idea
A husband owns the house but cannot sever family ties: he can block entry but not prevent seeing or talking.

In the chapter of Nafaqah, a critical balance emerges between the husband's property rights and the Islamic obligation to maintain family ties. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies that while the husband has authority over who enters his home, that authority does not extend to preventing his wife's relatives from seeing or speaking with her. The legal proof is a hadith warning against cutting family ties, and the operative fatwa specifies visit frequencies: weekly for parents, yearly for other mahram relatives.

Guided Path
1
State the husband's default authority
The passage begins by affirming the husband's absolute ownership of the house. He can prevent anyone from entering because it is his property. This is the baseline ruling.
Property rights are foundational in Hanafi fiqh; they are not absolute when they conflict with Shariah obligations.
2
Identify the exception for seeing and speaking
The commentary then qualifies that the husband cannot prevent the wife's parents or other relatives from seeing her or talking to her, because doing so would constitute cutting family ties (qati' al-rahim), which is haram. The proof is the hadith from Jubayr ibn Mut'im: 'The one who cuts family ties will not enter Paradise.'
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear: the prohibition of cutting ties is absolute.
3
Distinguish entry vs. staying overnight
Some scholars (mashayikh) add that the husband can prevent entry altogether? No, they say he can prevent staying overnight (if his fear of fitna is due to prolonged presence). The majority position is that he cannot prevent entry for seeing/talking, but he can limit the duration to avoid fitna from extended conversation.
This nuance shows that fitna is managed by limiting stay, not by severing contact entirely.
4
Apply the specified frequencies for regular visits
The text states the mufta bihi ruling: for parents, weekly visits (once a week); for other mahram relatives, yearly visits (once a year). This is the relied-upon fatwa from the later Hanafi masters.
The frequencies are not arbitrary; they balance the wife's right to maintain ties with the husband's right to privacy and protection from fitna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النفقة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
سے رو کے کیونکہ یہ گھر تو شوہر کی ملک ہے تو اس کو اپنی ملک میں آنے سے منع کرنے کا اختیار حاصل ہے اور بیوی کے والدین وغیہ وکو جب کبھی وہ چاہیں اس عورت کی طرف دیکھنے اور اس کے ساتھ باتیں کرنے سے منع نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس میں قطع رقم ہے اور شوہر کے حق میں کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے اور کہا گیا کہ آنے اور باتیں کرنے سے منع نہ کرے۔ البتہ شہر نے سے منع کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ فساد مظہر نے اور بہت دیر جیک باتیں کرنے میں ہے اور کہا گیا کہ عورت کو والدین کے پاس جانے اور اس کے پاس آنے سے ہر جمعہ میں (ایک بار) منع نہیں کر سکتا اور والدین کے ملا وہ دوسرے محارم کے ( حق ) میں اندازہ ایک سال ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے

اور والدین کے علاوہ دوسرے قرابت داروں کو سال میں ایک دفعہ ملاقات کرنے کی اجازت ہے خواہ عورت ان کے پاس جائے یا وہ یہاں آویں صحیح قول یہی ہے۔ بعض حضرات ایک ماہ میں ایک بار زیادہ کی اجازت دیتے ہیں۔
Chapter of maintenance. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya Volume 5. Because this house is the husband's property, so he has authority to prevent entry into his property. He should not prevent the wife's parents etc. from seeing her and speaking with her whenever they wish, because that causes cutting of ties and there is no harm to the husband. It has been said that he should not prevent entry and talking, but he can prevent staying overnight because evil and corruption appear in prolonged conversation. It has been said that he cannot prevent the wife from going to her parents' house and them coming to her once every Friday; and for other mahram relatives besides parents, the estimation is once a year, and that is correct. Explanation of the issue: The husband has authority to prevent the entry of his wife's mother, father, and her son from a previous husband, and other relatives, because this house is the husband's personal property, so he has authority to prevent entry. But if the wife's parents etc. want to see her or speak to her, the husband cannot prevent them from seeing her or speaking, because cutting family ties becomes necessary and cutting ties is haram. It is narrated from Jubayr ibn Mut'im that he heard the Prophet (PBUH) say: 'The one who cuts family ties will not enter Paradise.' And there is no harm to the husband in their seeing and speaking to her. Some scholars have said that just as he cannot prevent talking, he also cannot prevent entry. However, he can prevent them from staying, because if fitna and corruption occur, it happens from prolonged conversation. Most scholars have said that the wife going to her parents and them coming here once a week is not prevented, rather once a week meeting is allowed. This is the fatwa. And for relatives other than parents, once a year meeting is allowed, whether the wife goes to them or they come here. This is the correct saying. Some allow once a month or more.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is a ruling_with_proof from the Chapter of Nafaqah (Maintenance). The topic is the husband's authority over his house and its limits concerning visits by the wife's relatives. The passage first states the general principle: since the house is the husband's sole property, he has the right to prevent anyone from entering. However, this right is not absolute. The commentary then qualifies that the husband cannot prevent the wife's parents or other relatives from seeing the wife and talking with her, because doing so would constitute qati' al-rahim (cutting family ties), which is haram. The proof is a hadith from Jubayr ibn Mut'im that the cutter of family ties will not enter Paradise. There is no harm to the husband in visual or verbal contact. Some later scholars (mashayikh) added that the husband cannot even prevent entry, only overnight stay, because prolonged stay may cause fitna. The majority view, and the basis of fatwa, is that for parents, the wife may visit them and they may visit her once a week; for other mahram relatives, once a year. This balances the husband's property rights with the obligation to maintain family ties.

Key Terms
قطع رحم (qati' al-rahim): Severing family ties, such as preventing relatives from visiting or communicating.
محارم (mahram): Relatives with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as parents, siblings, and children.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is the mufta bihi ruling regarding visits by the wife's parents?
A) The husband can prevent them from entering the house at any time.
B) The husband cannot prevent them from visiting once a week.
C) The husband can prevent them from visiting if he fears fitna.
D) The husband can only allow them to visit once a year.

Key Takeaway
The husband's property rights are limited by the prohibition of cutting family ties: he may control entry to his house but cannot prevent seeing or talking, with specific visit frequencies for parents (weekly) and other mahram relatives (yearly).

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Setting Maintenance from Deposited Property: Conditions and Proof
Ruling on qadi setting maintenance from deposited property with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a qadi can set maintenance from an absent husband's property held by a depositary and explain the hadith proof for the wife's right to take maintenance.

Core Idea
The qadi sets maintenance from the absent's property when the depositary acknowledges the marriage; the wife's right is proven by the hadith of Hind.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling from Ashraf al-Hidayah on how a qadi provides for the dependents of an absent husband using property held in trust. The key is the depositary's acknowledgment or the qadi's own knowledge. We will also analyze the proof from the Sunnah that allows the wife to take her maintenance without explicit permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the absent husband and the property holder
The passage begins with a scenario: a husband (gha'ib) leaves property with a depositary (mudi'). The qadi can use that property for maintenance.
2
Understand the acknowledgment requirement
The depositary must acknowledge both the marriage and the deposit. Alternatively, if the qadi independently knows these facts, he may proceed without acknowledgment.
The depositary's acknowledgment is binding on himself, and it transfers to the absent's rights.
3
Apply the hadith proof
The wife's right to take maintenance from her husband's property without consent is proven by the hadith of Hind bint Utbah: 'Take from your husband's property what suffices you and your child in a reasonable manner.'
This hadith supports the general principle that a wife may take her due when the husband fails to provide.
4
Recognize extensions to other property types
The same ruling applies if the property is held as mudarabah (partnership) or if it is a debt owed to the absent.
The qadi can use these funds for maintenance under the same conditions.

درانحالیکہ مودع اور قرضدار دونوں اس بات کا اقرار کرتے ہیں کہ اس قرض خواہ کا غائب کے ذمہ قرضہ ہے اور ہمارے پاس غائب شخص کا مال بھی ہے تو قاضی اس مال ودیعت اور مال دین میں سے اس غائب کے قرضہ کو ادا کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیگا۔ حالانکہ بیوی بچوں کی طرح قرض خواہ کے قرضہ کی ادائیگی اس غائب شخص پر واجب ہے۔
The husband became absent; his property was with a man who acknowledges that this woman is his wife. Then the qadi will set maintenance for the absent man's wife, minor children, and parents from the property. And if a man is absent and has property with a man who acknowledges it and the marriage, the qadi will set maintenance for the absent's wife, minor children, and parents from that property. Likewise if the qadi knows that and he (the depositary) does not acknowledge it, because when he acknowledged the marriage and the deposit, he acknowledged her right to take from it, since she may take her right from her husband's property without his consent. The acknowledgment of the possessor is acceptable regarding himself, especially here, because if he denied either of the two matters, the woman's witnesses would not be accepted, for the depositary is not a defendant in proving marriage against him, nor is the woman a plaintiff in proving the absent's rights. So when it is established regarding him, it transfers to the absent. Likewise if the property is in his hand as mudarabah, and the same answer regarding debt. All this is when the property is of the same type as her right: dirhams, dinars, food, or clothing of the type of her right. But if it is of a different type, maintenance is not set because it needs to be sold, and the property of an absent person is not sold unanimously. According to Abu Hanifa, because it is not sold regarding a present person, and similarly regarding an absent. According to the two, because although he gives judgment against the present because his refusal is known, he does not give judgment against the absent because his refusal is not known. Translation: And if a man becomes absent and his property is in the possession of a person who acknowledges it and also acknowledges that this woman is the wife of that absent person, then the qadi will set from that property maintenance for the absent's wife, his minor children, and his parents. Similarly if the qadi himself knows that, even if the depositary did not acknowledge it. Because when the depositary acknowledged both marriage and deposit, he also acknowledged that the wife has the right to take from it, since the wife has the authority to take her right from her husband's property without his consent. The acknowledgment of the possessor is acceptable regarding himself, especially here, because if he denied either of the two matters, the woman's witnesses would not be accepted. For the depositary cannot be a defendant in proving marriage against him, nor can the woman be a plaintiff in proving the absent's rights. So when it is established regarding him, it transfers to the absent. Similarly if the property is in his hand as mudarabah, and the same rule applies to debt. All this detail is when the property is of the same type as her right: rupees, gold coins, grain, or clothing of the type of her right. But if the property is of a different type, the qadi will not set maintenance because it needs to be sold, and the absent's property is not sold by agreement. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the present person's property is not sold, and similarly the absent's. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because although the qadi gives judgment against the present because his refusal is known, he will not give judgment against the absent because his refusal is not known. Explanation of the issue: If the husband left on a journey and some of his property is with a person, e.g., Hamid, who acknowledges the deposit and that this woman is the absent's wife, then the qadi will set maintenance for the absent's wife, minor children, and parents from that property. Similarly if the qadi himself knows that this is his wife and his property with Hamid, even if Hamid did not acknowledge that this woman is the absent's wife and that he has his deposit, then also the qadi will set maintenance. The proof is that when Hamid acknowledged both marriage and deposit, he also acknowledged that the wife has the right to take from this property. Because the wife has the authority to take her need from her husband's property without his consent, as indicated by the hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) told Hind, wife of Abu Sufyan: 'Take from your husband's property what suffices you and your child in a reasonable manner.' Here an objection arises: If a creditor demands from the absent's depositary or debtor his debt while both acknowledge that the creditor has a debt on the absent and they have the absent's property, the qadi will not order payment of the debt from that property, even though debt repayment is obligatory on the absent just like maintenance for wife and children.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is a ruling_with_proof from the Chapter of Nafaqah, addressing the situation of an absent husband (gha'ib) who leaves property in the custody of someone (mudi'/depositary). The main ruling: If the depositary acknowledges both the deposit and that the woman is the absent's wife, the qadi can set maintenance for the wife, minor children, and parents from that property. The same applies if the qadi independently knows these facts even without the depositary's acknowledgment. The proof is twofold: first, the wife has a general right to take her maintenance from her husband's property without his permission, as derived from the hadith of Hind bint Utbah; second, the depositary's acknowledgment is binding regarding himself, and since it establishes the marriage and deposit, it transfers to the absent. The passage then discusses conditions: the property must be of the same type as the maintenance (e.g., dirhams, food, clothing). If it is of a different type, the qadi cannot set maintenance because it would require selling the property of the absent, which is prohibited by consensus. Here an intra-Hanafi dispute emerges: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that property of an absent person cannot be sold at all, just as it cannot be sold for a present person. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that for a present person, the qadi can sell if the person refuses to pay, but for an absent, since his refusal is unknown, it cannot be sold. This distinction prevents the qadi from selling property of a different type to provide maintenance. Finally, an objection is raised: why can the qadi allocate maintenance to dependents but not repay a debt? The text does not resolve this, leaving it as an apparent inconsistency. The Hanafi position is that maintenance takes precedence due to the urgent need of dependents.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): A husband who is absent, such that his whereabouts and ability to provide maintenance are unknown.
مودع (mudi'): The person with whom the absent husband's property is deposited (depositary).
مضاربت (mudarabah): A partnership contract where one party provides capital and the other labor, profit shared as agreed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary proof that a wife can take maintenance from her absent husband's property without his permission?
A) The consensus of the Sahibayn
B) The hadith of Hind bint Utbah
C) The qiyas on debt repayment
D) The principle of istihsan

Key Takeaway
The qadi can set maintenance for dependents from an absent husband's deposited property when the depositary acknowledges the marriage or the qadi knows it, based on the wife's right to take without permission as proven by the hadith of Hind.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition on Selling Absent's Property: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Condition on property type and intra-Hanafi dispute on selling absent's property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's reasoning for prohibiting the sale of an absent person's property, and state the practical consequence for setting maintenance.

Core Idea
Absent's property of a different type cannot be sold for maintenance; Abu Hanifa forbids all sales, the Sahibayn allow for present but not absent due to unknown refusal.

This lesson focuses on the condition that the absent's property must be of the same type as the maintenance. If it is of a different type, the qadi cannot set maintenance because selling the property is required and that is prohibited. We explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement on why selling is forbidden, which leads to the same practical outcome but different legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of same-type property
The passage states: 'وهذا كله اذاكان المال من جنس حقها' – all the previous rulings apply when the property is of the same type as the maintenance (e.g., cash, food, clothing).
2
Understand why different-type property requires sale
If the property is of a different type (e.g., land, livestock), it cannot be used directly for maintenance; it must be sold to convert to the needed type. But selling the absent's property is forbidden.
The prohibition is unanimous among the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa says the property of an absent person is not sold just as the property of a present person is not sold. He draws an analogy: since a present person's property cannot be sold without his explicit order, the same applies to an absent person.
This is a strict view: no one is sold property.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn distinguish between present and absent. For a present person, the qadi can sell if the person refuses to pay, because his refusal is known. For an absent, his refusal is unknown, so selling is not permitted.
Their reasoning gives a conditional allowance for present but not absent.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Both views lead to the same result: the qadi cannot set maintenance from different-type property because selling is not allowed. The difference is in the underlying principle.
This is an example of a legitimate ikhtilaf that does not affect the fatwa.

تو اس نے یہ بھی اقرار کیا کہ بیوی کو اس مال سے ) لینے کا حق ہے کیونکہ بیوی کو اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ شوہر کے مال سے بغیر شوہر کی رضا مندی کے اپنا حق لے لے اور صاحب قبضہ کا اقرار اپنے حق میں مقبول ہے خصوصاً اس مقام پر اس لئے کہ اگر وہ دونوں امروں میں کسی ایک کا انکار کرتا تو اس پر عورت کے گواہ قبول نہ ہوتے۔ کیونکہ غائب شخص پر زوجیت ثابت کرنے کے واسطے ودیعت رکھنے والا مدعی علیہ نہیں ہو سکتا اور نہ مرد غائب حقوق ثابت کرنے میں اس کی بیوی مدعی ہو سکتی ہے۔ پس جب اس حق میں ( یہ امر ) ثابت ہو گیا تو غائب کے حق میں بھی متعدی ہوگا اور اسی طرح اگر اس شخص کے قبضہ میں ( یہ مال ) بطور مضاربت ہو اور یہی حکم غائب کے قرضہ میں ہے اور یہ سب تفصیل اس وقت ہے جبکہ عورت کے حق کی جنس سے ہو۔ روپیہ اشرفی اناج یا عورت کے حق کی جنس کا کپڑا ہو۔ البتہ اگر یہ مال خلاف جنس ہو، تو قاضی اس میں نفقہ مقرر نہیں کرے گا۔ کیوں کہ اس کے بیچنے کی ضرورت ہے اور غائب کا مال بالا نفاق نہیں بیچا جاتا ہے۔ سوامام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ حاضر کا مال نہیں بیچا جاتا اور ایسے ہی غائب کا اور ربا صاحبین کے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ قاضی اگر چہ حاضر پر ( اس کا مال فروخت کرنے کا حکم دیتا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ حاضر کا انکار کرنا قاضی کو معلوم ہو جاتا ہے غائب پر ( یہ حکم ) نہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اس کا انکار کرنا معلوم نہیں ہوا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر سفر میں چلا گیا اور اس کا کچھ مال کسی شخص مثلاً حامد کے قبضہ میں ہے جو اس دویعت کا اقرار کرتا ہے کہ یہ عورت اس غائب مرد کی بیوی سے تو قاضی اس مال میں سے اس غائب کی بیوی اور اس کی نابالغ اولا د اور ا سکے والدین کا نفقہ مقرر کر دے گا اور اسی طرح اگر قاضی کو خود یہ بات معلوم ہے کہ یہ صورت اس کی بیوٹی ہے اور اس کا مال حامد کے پاس ہے ۔ حالانکہ حامد نے اس کا اقرار نہیں کیا کہ یہ عورت اس غائب کی بیوی ہے اور میرے پاس اس کا نال دو بیعت ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی قاضی اس مال سے غائب کی بیوی اور نابالغ بچوں اور اس کے والدین کا نفقہ مقرر کر دے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب حامد نے زوجیت اور ودیعت دونوں کا اقرار کیا تو اس نے یہ بھی اقرار کیا کہ بیوی کو اس مال سے لینے کا حق ہے۔ کیونکہ بیوی کو اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ شوہر کے مال سے بغیر اس کی رضامندی کے بقدر ضرورت لے لے اور اس پر دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں ابوسفیان کی بیوی ہندہ سے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا تھا ــدى مــن مـــال زوجک مایکفیک وولدك بالمعروف - یہاں ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر قرض خواہ نے غائب کے مودع یا قرضدار سے اپنے قرضہ کا مطالبہ کیا درانحالیکہ مودع اور قرضدار دونوں اس بات کا اقرار کرتے ہیں کہ اس قرض خواہ کا غائب کے ذمہ قرضہ ہے اور ہمارے پاس غائب شخص کا مال بھی ہے تو قاضی اس مال ودیعت اور مال دین میں سے اس غائب کے قرضہ کو ادا کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیگا۔ حالانکہ بیوی بچوں کی طرح قرض خواہ کے قرضہ کی ادائیگی اس غائب شخص پر واجب ہے۔
The husband became absent; his property was with a man who acknowledges that this woman is his wife. Then the qadi will set maintenance for the absent man's wife, minor children, and parents from the property. And if a man is absent and has property with a man who acknowledges it and the marriage, the qadi will set maintenance for the absent's wife, minor children, and parents from that property. Likewise if the qadi knows that and he (the depositary) does not acknowledge it, because when he acknowledged the marriage and the deposit, he acknowledged her right to take from it, since she may take her right from her husband's property without his consent. The acknowledgment of the possessor is acceptable regarding himself, especially here, because if he denied either of the two matters, the woman's witnesses would not be accepted, for the depositary is not a defendant in proving marriage against him, nor is the woman a plaintiff in proving the absent's rights. So when it is established regarding him, it transfers to the absent. Likewise if the property is in his hand as mudarabah, and the same answer regarding debt. All this is when the property is of the same type as her right: dirhams, dinars, food, or clothing of the type of her right. But if it is of a different type, maintenance is not set because it needs to be sold, and the property of an absent person is not sold unanimously. According to Abu Hanifa, because it is not sold regarding a present person, and similarly regarding an absent. According to the two, because although he gives judgment against the present because his refusal is known, he does not give judgment against the absent because his refusal is not known. Translation: And if a man becomes absent and his property is in the possession of a person who acknowledges it and also acknowledges that this woman is the wife of that absent person, then the qadi will set from that property maintenance for the absent's wife, his minor children, and his parents. Similarly if the qadi himself knows that, even if the depositary did not acknowledge it. Because when the depositary acknowledged both marriage and deposit, he also acknowledged that the wife has the right to take from it, since the wife has the authority to take her right from her husband's property without his consent. The acknowledgment of the possessor is acceptable regarding himself, especially here, because if he denied either of the two matters, the woman's witnesses would not be accepted. For the depositary cannot be a defendant in proving marriage against him, nor can the woman be a plaintiff in proving the absent's rights. So when it is established regarding him, it transfers to the absent. Similarly if the property is in his hand as mudarabah, and the same rule applies to debt. All this detail is when the property is of the same type as her right: rupees, gold coins, grain, or clothing of the type of her right. But if the property is of a different type, the qadi will not set maintenance because it needs to be sold, and the absent's property is not sold by agreement. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the present person's property is not sold, and similarly the absent's. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because although the qadi gives judgment against the present because his refusal is known, he will not give judgment against the absent because his refusal is not known. Explanation of the issue: If the husband left on a journey and some of his property is with a person, e.g., Hamid, who acknowledges the deposit and that this woman is the absent's wife, then the qadi will set maintenance for the absent's wife, minor children, and parents from that property. Similarly if the qadi himself knows that this is his wife and his property with Hamid, even if Hamid did not acknowledge that this woman is the absent's wife and that he has his deposit, then also the qadi will set maintenance. The proof is that when Hamid acknowledged both marriage and deposit, he also acknowledged that the wife has the right to take from this property. Because the wife has the authority to take her need from her husband's property without his consent, as indicated by the hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) told Hind, wife of Abu Sufyan: 'Take from your husband's property what suffices you and your child in a reasonable manner.' Here an objection arises: If a creditor demands from the absent's depositary or debtor his debt while both acknowledge that the creditor has a debt on the absent and they have the absent's property, the qadi will not order payment of the debt from that property, even though debt repayment is obligatory on the absent just like maintenance for wife and children.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is a ruling_with_proof from the Chapter of Nafaqah, addressing the situation of an absent husband (gha'ib) who leaves property in the custody of someone (mudi'/depositary). The main ruling: If the depositary acknowledges both the deposit and that the woman is the absent's wife, the qadi can set maintenance for the wife, minor children, and parents from that property. The same applies if the qadi independently knows these facts even without the depositary's acknowledgment. The proof is twofold: first, the wife has a general right to take her maintenance from her husband's property without his permission, as derived from the hadith of Hind bint Utbah; second, the depositary's acknowledgment is binding regarding himself, and since it establishes the marriage and deposit, it transfers to the absent. The passage then discusses conditions: the property must be of the same type as the maintenance (e.g., dirhams, food, clothing). If it is of a different type, the qadi cannot set maintenance because it would require selling the property of the absent, which is prohibited by consensus. Here an intra-Hanafi dispute emerges: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that property of an absent person cannot be sold at all, just as it cannot be sold for a present person. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that for a present person, the qadi can sell if the person refuses to pay, but for an absent, since his refusal is unknown, it cannot be sold. This distinction prevents the qadi from selling property of a different type to provide maintenance. Finally, an objection is raised: why can the qadi allocate maintenance to dependents but not repay a debt? The text does not resolve this, leaving it as an apparent inconsistency. The Hanafi position is that maintenance takes precedence due to the urgent need of dependents.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): A husband who is absent, such that his whereabouts and ability to provide maintenance are unknown.
جنس الحق (jins al-haqq): The type or category of the maintenance right (e.g., cash, food, clothing).
بيع مال الغائب (bay' mal al-gha'ib): Selling the property of an absent person without his explicit permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the practical outcome for setting maintenance when the absent husband's property is of a different type from the maintenance?
A) The qadi can sell the property to provide maintenance.
B) The qadi does not set maintenance because selling the absent's property is prohibited.
C) The wife can sell the property herself.
D) The qadi can only set maintenance if the property is cash.

Key Takeaway
The absent's property cannot be sold for maintenance if it is of a different type, a ruling upheld by both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn with different reasoning but same practical effect.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
12 min
Maintenance for Absent Husband's Family from Deposited Property
Ruling on qadi ordering maintenance from absent's property held by another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge can order maintenance from an absent husband's property held by a depositary, and explain why the judge cannot sell that property.

Core Idea
Wife's right to maintenance extends to absent husband's deposit, but judge cannot sell property of different type.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the chapter of maintenance (nafaqah) regarding an absent husband whose property is in the custody of a depositary. The judge may order maintenance for the wife, children, and parents, but only if the property matches the type of the wife's right. We will also explore the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the judge can sell the absent's property to fulfill obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and parties
Determine the situation: an absent husband, his property held by a depositary, and the wife claiming maintenance. Understand who the depositary is and what he admits.
The depositary's admission or the judge's personal knowledge is key.
2
Understand the condition for the judge's order
The judge can order maintenance only if the property is of the same type as the wife's right (e.g., currency, grain, or clothing). If it is a different type (e.g., house, slave), the judge cannot order because selling would be required.
This condition prevents selling the absent's property, which is prohibited.
3
Analyze the proof from hadith
The hadith of Hind bint Utbah (خذي من مال زوجك ما يكفيك) is cited to show the wife's right to take from her husband's property without consent. This right extends to the judge ordering from the absent's property.
The imperative indicates permissibility, and the Hanafi school applies it generally.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on selling
Imam Abu Hanifa says the judge cannot sell the absent's property because he cannot even sell a present person's property. The Sahibayn say the judge can sell a present person's property if he refuses, but cannot sell an absent's because his refusal is unknown. The consensus (bil-ittifaq) is that selling is not allowed.
The thamarah (practical consequence) is that if the property is of a different type, no maintenance can be ordered.
5
Apply the ruling to distinguish between maintenance and debt
The judge can order maintenance for dependents because it preserves the absent's ownership (beneficial to him), but cannot order payment of debts because that would be against his interests without benefit.
This distinction is based on 'kindness and consideration' for the absent.

باقی رکھنا نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ ایک اجنبی کے کہنے سے اس کے خلاف حکم کرنا ہے پس اس فرق کی وجہ سے قاضی بیوی بچوں کے واسطے نفقہ کا حکم کرسکتا ہے۔ مگر قرضہ ادا کرنے کا حکم نہیں کر سکتا۔ واقرار صاحب الید سے بھی ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ جس شخص کے پاس غائب شخص کا مال ودیعت ہے اس کا اقرار صحیح نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ یہ اقرار علی الغائب ( غائب کے خلاف اقرار کرنا ) ہے۔ جواب قابیض یعنی جسکے پاس غائب کا مال ودیعت ہے اس کا اقرار اپنے حق میں مقبول ہے حضوصاً اس مقام پر۔ کیونکہ اگر وہ زوجیت یا ودیعت میں سے کسی امر کا انکار کرتا تو اس پر عورت کے گواہ قبول نہ ہوتے۔ کیونکہ عورت کا بینہ اگر زوجیت اور نکاح ثابت کرنے کے لئے ہے تو اس لئے قبول نہیں ہوگا۔ کہ مودع ( ودیعت رکھنے والا ) نائب شخص پر نکاح ثابت کرنے میں مدعی علیہ نہیں ہوسکتا اور اگر عورت نے ودیعت پر بعینہ قائم کیا ہے تو اس لئے قبول نہیں ہوگا۔ کہ مرد غائب کے حقوق ثابت کرنے میں وہ مدعی نہیں ہو سکتی ہے ۔ بہر حال جب عورت کے گواہ قبول نہیں ہوئے تو مودع ( ودیعت رکھنے والے کا) اقرار ضرور قبول ہوگا۔ پس جب مودع کا اقرار خود اس کے حق میں ثابت ہو گیا تو غائب کے حق میں بھی متعدی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مودع نے جس چیز کا اقرار کیا ہے وہ اس مرد غائب کی ملک ہے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کہ ایک مرد نے رمضان کا چاند دیکھا تو پہلے اس کے حق میں رمضان ہونا ثابت ہوگا ۔ پھر اس کے علاوہ کی طرف متعدی ہوگا اور یہی حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ مال اس شخص کے پاس بطور مضاربت ہو۔ یعنی اگر قابض اس مال مضاربت کا اور زوجیت کا اقرار کرتا ہے یا قاضی کو ذاتی علم ہو تو قاضی اس مال مضاربت میں سے ان لوگوں کا نفقہ مقرر کر دے گا اور اسی طرح اگر اس شخص پر غائب آدمی کا قرضہ ہے، اور یہ اس قرضہ اور زوجیت کا اقرار کرے یا قاضی کو ذاتی علم ہو تو بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ یعنی قاضی اس مال میں سے ان لوگوں کا نفقہ مقرر دے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ سب تفصیل اس صورت میں ہے کہ یہ مال عورت کے حق کی جنس سے ہو۔ مثلا روپے ہوں یا اشرفیاں یا اناج یا عورت کے حق کی جنس کا لباس ہو ۔ یعنی جیسا کپڑا اس عورت کیلئے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اگر اسی جنس کا کپڑا حامد کے پاس ودیعت ہو، تو قاضی اس میں سے کپڑا دلوا دے گا اور اگر یہ مال عورت کے حق کی جنس کے خلاف ہو۔ مثلاً مکان غلام یا دیگر سامان ودیعت رکھ گیا ہو تو قاضی اس میں سے نفقہ مقررنہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ نفقہ دینے کے واسطے اس کے بیچنے کی ضرورت ہے اور غائب کا مال بالا تفاق نہیں بیچا جاتا ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر وہ شخص موجود ہوتا اور حاضر ہوتا تو قاضی کو اس کا مال بیچے کا اختیار نہ ہوتا۔ کیونکہ قاضی کی بیع اسلئے درست ہوتی ہے کہ مالک کو بیع کرنے سے روک دیا گیا ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک آزاد عاقل بالغ کو بیچ کرنے سے روکنا باطل ہے۔ پس جب حاضر کا مال نہیں بیچا جا سکتا تو غائب کا بدرجہ اولیٰ نہیں بیچا جائے گا۔ اور رہا صاحبین کے نزدیک تو اس واسطے کہ قاضی اگر چہ حاضر پر اس کا مال فروخت کرنے کا حکم دے سکتا ہے اس وجہ سے کہ ادائے حق سے انکار کرنا قاضی کو معلوم ہو جاتا ہے اور ادائے حق سے انکار کرنا ہی قاضی کیلئے جواز بیع کی شرط ہے۔ لیکن غائب پر یہ حکم نہیں کرے گا کیونکہ غائب کا ادائے حق سے انکار کرنا قاضی کو معلوم نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ ادائے حق سے انکار کرنا ہی جواز بیع کی شرط ہے۔
Chapter of Maintenance. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume Five. The property of an absent person is not sold by consensus. According to Abu Hanifa, because it is not sold against a present person, similarly against an absent. According to the two (Sahibayn), because (the judge) can order against a present person because his refusal is known, but cannot order against an absent because his refusal is not known. Translation: And if a man went absent and his property is in the possession of a person who admits it and (also admits that) this woman is the wife of that absent person, then the judge will fix maintenance from that property for the wife of that absent person, his minor children, and his parents. Similarly if the judge himself knows this, even if the depositary has not admitted it. Because when the depositary admitted both marriage and deposit, he also admitted that the wife has the right to take from this property, because the wife has the authority to take her right from the husband's property without the husband's consent. And the admission of the possessor is accepted regarding his own right, especially in this place, because if he denied either of the two matters, then the wife's witnesses would not be accepted against him. Because the depositary cannot be a defendant in proving marriage against the absent person, nor can the wife be a plaintiff in proving the rights of the absent man. So when this right is established, it becomes valid against the absent person. And similarly if this property is in that person's possession as mudarabah, and the same ruling applies to the absent person's debt. And all this detail applies when (the property) is of the same type as the wife's right: rupees, gold dinars, grain, or cloth of the same type as the wife's right. But if this property is of a different type, then the judge will not fix maintenance from it, because it needs to be sold, and the absent person's property is not sold by consensus. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the property of a present person is not sold, and similarly of an absent. According to the two, because the judge can order (the sale) against a present person because his refusal becomes known, but cannot order against an absent because his refusal is not known. Explanation of the issue: If the husband went on a journey and some of his property is in the possession of a person, e.g., Hamid, who admits the deposit and that this woman is the wife of that absent man, then the judge will fix maintenance from that property for the absent's wife, his minor children, and his parents. Similarly, if the judge himself knows that this is his wife and his property is with Hamid, even if Hamid has not admitted that this woman is the absent's wife and that he has his deposit, then too the judge will fix maintenance from that property for the absent's wife, minor children, and parents. The proof is that when Hamid admitted both marriage and deposit, he also admitted that the wife has the right to take from this property. Because the wife has the authority to take from the husband's property without his consent to the extent of need. The proof for this is the hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Hind, the wife of Abu Sufyan: 'Take from your husband's property what suffices you and your children in a reasonable manner.' There is an objection here: If a creditor demands his debt from the absent's depositary or debtor, while both the depositary and debtor admit that the creditor has a debt on the absent and that they have the absent's property, then the judge will not order payment of the absent's debt from the deposited property or debt property, even though payment of the creditor's debt is obligatory on the absent person just like the wife and children. The answer is that the judge can only order something that is beneficial and useful for the absent person; regarding something that does not involve kindness and consideration for the absent, the judge is not authorized to order. So ordering maintenance for the wife and children involves kindness to the absent man because his ownership remains intact, but in paying the debt, his ownership is not preserved; rather, it is issuing a ruling against him at the behest of a stranger. Due to this difference, the judge can order maintenance for the wife and children but cannot order payment of the debt. And there is also an answer to a question regarding the admission of the person in possession. The question is: The admission of the person who has the absent's property as deposit should not be valid because it is an admission against the absent. The answer: The admission of the person in possession, i.e., the one who has the absent's property as deposit, is accepted regarding his own right, especially in this place. Because if he denied either marriage or deposit, the wife's witnesses would not be accepted against him. Because if the wife's evidence is to prove marriage and (the depositary) cannot be a defendant in proving marriage against the absent person, and if the wife established the deposit itself, her evidence would not be accepted because she cannot be a plaintiff in proving the rights of the absent man. In any case, when the wife's witnesses are not accepted, the admission of the depositary must be accepted. So when the depositary's admission is established regarding his own right, it becomes valid against the absent person as well, because what the depositary admitted is the property of that absent man. This is like when a man sees the moon of Ramadan: first Ramadan is established for him, then it becomes valid for others. And this same ruling applies when the property is in that person's possession as mudarabah. That is, if the possessor admits this mudarabah property and the marriage, or the judge has personal knowledge, the judge will fix maintenance from this mudarabah property for these people. Similarly, if that person owes a debt to the absent man, and he admits this debt and the marriage, or the judge has personal knowledge, the same ruling applies: the judge will fix maintenance from this property for these people. The author of al-Hidayah says: All these details apply when this property is of the same type as the wife's right. For example, if it is rupees, gold dinars, grain, or clothing of the same type as the wife's right. That is, the kind of cloth that is obligatory for this woman. If that kind of cloth is deposited with Hamid, the judge will order delivery of cloth from it. If this property is contrary to the type of the wife's right, for example, a house, a slave, or other goods deposited, then the judge will not fix maintenance from it, because to give maintenance it needs to be sold, and the absent person's property is not sold by consensus. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that if that person were present, the judge would not have the authority to sell his property, because the judge's sale is valid only when the owner is prevented from selling, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, preventing a free, sane, adult from selling is invalid. So when the property of a present person cannot be sold, then the property of an absent person is even more so not sold. As for the two (Sahibayn), it is because the judge can order the sale of the property of a present person because his refusal to fulfill the right becomes known to the judge, and refusal to fulfill the right is the condition for the permissibility of the sale. But he will not order this against an absent person because the absent's refusal to fulfill the right is not known to the judge, even though refusal to fulfill the right is the condition for the permissibility of the sale.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on maintenance (nafaqah). It discusses the case of an absent husband (gha'ib) whose property is in the custody of another person (mudi' or depositary). The judge (qadi) is permitted to order maintenance for the wife, minor children, and parents from that property if the depositary admits both the deposit and the marriage, or if the judge has personal knowledge. The proof is that the wife has the right to take from her husband's property for her needs without his consent, as established by the hadith of Hind bint Utbah. However, the judge cannot order payment of debts from this property because that would not be beneficial to the absent person (his ownership would not be preserved). The depositary's admission is accepted regarding his own right; if he denied either, the wife's witnesses would not be accepted because she cannot be plaintiff against the absent nor can the depositary be defendant in proving marriage. The passage also conditions that the property must be of the same type as the wife's right (e.g., currency, grain, or clothing); if it is of a different type (e.g., a house or slave), the judge cannot order maintenance because selling the property is required, and the absent's property cannot be sold. This leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that since a present person's property cannot be sold by the judge, the absent's property even more so cannot be sold. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that a judge can sell the property of a present person who refuses to pay, but cannot sell an absent person's property because his refusal is unknown. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school for selling against an absent is that it is not permitted, as per the text.

Key Terms
مودع (mudi'): The person who deposits property; the depositary in this context is the one holding the absent person's property.
غائب (gha'ib): An absent person whose whereabouts are unknown or who is not present in the jurisdiction.
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, for the wife, minor children, and parents.
قاضي (qadi): A judge appointed by the state who can order maintenance from an absent person's property under certain conditions.
باع (ba'a): To sell. The text discusses the sale of property by the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for the judge to order maintenance from the absent husband's property held by a depositary?
A) The property must be of the same type as the wife's right (e.g., currency or clothing).
B) The depositary must be a relative of the absent.
C) The wife must have witnesses to the marriage.
D) The absent husband must have explicitly authorized the sale.

Key Takeaway
The judge can order maintenance from an absent's property only if it is of the same type as the wife's right; selling the absent's property is prohibited by consensus.
