Father hiring a wet nurse. He (al-Quduri) said: The father hires one who will breastfeed the child at her (the mother's) place. As for the father hiring, it is because the payment is upon him. And his saying 'at her place' means when she (the mother) wishes that, because custody belongs to her. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The father hires a woman to breastfeed the child at the mother's place. So the father's hiring is because the payment is obligatory on the father. And what he said that she breastfeeds at her mother's place, its meaning is when the mother wishes that, because the right of custody is for the mother. Commentary: The issue is that the father hires a woman for breastfeeding who will stay at the child's mother's place and breastfeed. As for the fact that the father will hire the wet nurse, it is because the payment is obligatory on the father. And what al-Quduri said that the wet nurse breastfeeds at the mother's place, its meaning is that if the mother wishes, the wet nurse must breastfeed at her place, because the right of upbringing is for the mother.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar that the father hires a wet nurse for the child, and she breastfeeds at the mother's home if the mother desires. The justification is that the father is responsible for maintenance (including breastfeeding expenses), and the mother has the right of custody (hadana) and upbringing, so the breastfeeding should take place in her home unless she agrees otherwise. The commentary clarifies that it is not necessary for the mother to breastfeed herself; she can delegate, but the wet nurse must come to her. This ruling is based on the principle that custody rights belong to the mother, so the child should not be taken away from her. The authority weight is from Mukhtasar al-Quduri, which is a foundational Hanafi matn.

Key Terms
مرضعة (murdi'ah): Wet nurse hired to breastfeed the child.
حجر (hajr): Right of custody; the mother's right to keep the child in her care.

Hiring Wife or Mu'taddah to Breastfeed: Hanafi Ruling and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring one's wife or mu'taddah to breastfeed their joint child and distinguish the two narrations for ba'in divorce, applying the concept of diyanatan.

Core Idea
A mother's breastfeeding of her own child is a wajib duty; she cannot be paid for it.

This lesson addresses a specific but important family-law issue: Can a husband pay his wife or former wife in her waiting period to breastfeed their child? The text establishes the general rule and then unpacks an internal Hanafi disagreement when the divorce is irreversible. Understanding this ruling requires applying the principle that a wajib act cannot be compensated if payment is for the obligation itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The act is a hiring contract (ijarah) where the husband hires a woman to breastfeed his child. The women considered are: his current wife, his wife in revocable iddah, and his wife in irreversible iddah (mabtutah).
The child is joint – the woman is the biological mother.
2
State the general ruling and its basis
The matn rules that hiring is not permissible because breastfeeding is wajib diyanatan (religiously obligatory) upon the mother. The Quranic proof is cited (2:233), interpreted as a command.
'Diyanatan' means binding before Allah, not enforceable in court.
3
Examine the wajh al-dalalah
The verse uses the indicative 'yurdi'na' but is understood as an imperative (amr) due to legislative context. Since the mother was excused only due to possible inability, accepting payment proves ability, so the obligation is confirmed and payment is forbidden.
This reasoning relies on Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub when no contrary evidence.
4
Distinguish between types of iddah
For revocable divorce (raj'i), the ruling is unanimous – the marriage continues, so the obligation remains. For ba'in divorce, there is an ikhtilaf within the madhhab.
Revocable divorce: husband can take her back without a new contract; marriage persists.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
In one narration, hiring is invalid (first opinion) because some effects of marriage remain (iddah, nafaqah, housing). In the other, it is permissible because the marriage bond is severed. The first is more cautious and often preferred by later scholars.
The thamarah (practical consequence) is whether the contract is valid or not.

And if he hires her while she is his wife or his mu'taddah to breastfeed his child, it is not permissible because breastfeeding is wajib upon her diyanatan. Allah Most High said: 'And mothers shall breastfeed their children.' Except that she was excused due to the possibility of her inability. So when she undertakes it with payment, her ability becomes apparent, so the action becomes wajib upon her, so it is not permissible to take payment for it. And this (non-permissibility of hiring) in the 'iddah of a revocable divorce is a single narration (unanimous), because the marriage remains. And likewise in the ba'in divorce in one narration. In another narration, hiring her is permissible because the marriage has ceased. The first opinion is that it remains in effect for some rulings. In the commentary: The issue is that if the husband hires his child's mother to breastfeed while she is his wife or in his 'iddah, it is not permissible. Because diyanatan breastfeeding is wajib upon her. Allah said: 'And mothers shall breastfeed their children.' The verb 'yurdi'na' is in the indicative mood but in the meaning of command, like 'yatarabbasna' in 'And divorced women shall wait...' But she was excused due to possibility of inability. So when she undertakes with payment, her ability becomes apparent, so breastfeeding becomes wajib upon her by Allah's command, thus taking payment is not permissible. And this ruling of non-permissibility is unanimous for revocable divorce because marriage remains. For ba'in divorce, there are two narrations: one says not permissible because remnants of marriage exist (like 'iddah, nafaqah, housing), another says permissible because marriage has ceased.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a husband paying his wife or a woman in her 'iddah (waiting period) to breastfeed their own child. The matn states it is not permissible because breastfeeding is wajib diyanatan upon the mother. The proof is the Quranic verse: 'And mothers shall breastfeed their children' (2:233). Although the verse is in the indicative form, it is interpreted as a command due to the context. The mother was initially excused if she was unable, but by accepting payment, she demonstrates her ability, so the obligation becomes established, and she cannot take payment. The commentary then distinguishes between types of 'iddah: For revocable divorce (raj'i), it is unanimous that hiring is invalid because the marriage continues. For irreducible divorce (ba'in), there is disagreement among Hanafi authorities: in one narration, it is also invalid because some effects of marriage remain (like 'iddah, maintenance, housing). In another narration, it is permissible because the marriage has ended. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is typically the first, but both are transmitted. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The underlying principle is that a wajib act cannot be compensated if payment would be for a religious obligation.

Key Terms
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman in her waiting period (iddah) after divorce or death.
مبتوتة (mabtutah): A woman who has been given a ba'in (irreducible) divorce.
ديانة (diyanatan): In conscience; a religious obligation that is not enforceable by court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mother's breastfeeding of her own child is a religious obligation; she cannot accept payment for it from the father.

Hiring Wife to Breastfeed Another Wife's Child
Ruling on hiring a wife to breastfeed a step-child from another wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring one’s wife to breastfeed a child from another wife and explain the legal basis for the permissibility.

Core Idea
You can pay your wife for breastfeeding another wife’s child because she owes no duty to that child.

This passage clarifies an important exception within the rules of breastfeeding contracts. While a wife cannot be paid for nursing her own child (since that is wajib upon her), she may be hired to nurse the husband’s child from another woman. The ruling is based on the principle that payment is permissible only for services that are not legally obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
What is the legal act described? A husband hires his wife (or mu'taddah) to breastfeed a child that is not her own. What is the ruling? It is permissible (jā'iz).
2
Locate the Legal Basis
The passage states the reason: 'because it is not wajib upon her'. Identify the principle: payment for a service is valid only if the service is not a legal obligation (wajib) on the performer.
3
Contrast with the Impermissible Case
Compare with the case where the wife is hired to breastfeed her own child. Why is that invalid? Because she is already obligated to nurse her own child (wajib), and payment for a wajib act is not valid in Hanafi fiqh.
This distinction is key to understanding the ruling.
4
Note the Scope of the Ruling
The ruling applies whether the woman is still a wife (mankuha) or in her 'iddah period (mu'taddah). Also, it applies to a child from another wife—not necessarily the husband's child from a previous marriage? The text says 'ibn lahu min ghayriha' implying a child of the husband from another woman.
The woman's status does not affect the permissibility.
5
Confirm the Hanafi Position
This is the established position from Zahir al-Riwayah, as recorded in Al-Hidayah. There is no significant intra-Hanafi dispute on this point.

Source Text

Commentary
This short passage makes an exception to the previous rule. While a wife cannot be hired to breastfeed her own child (because it is wajib upon her), she can be hired to breastfeed the husband's child from another woman. The reasoning is that she has no parental obligation towards that child, so breastfeeding becomes a service for which she can validly receive payment. This is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that one cannot take payment for a wajib act, but can for voluntary acts. The commentary notes that the proof is clear: the lack of obligation. This ruling applies whether the woman is a wife or in 'iddah (revocable or ba'in), as the text uses 'mankuha aw mu'taddahu'. The authority weight is from the commentary of Hidayah.

Hiring Mother After 'Iddah Expires is Permissible
Ruling that a mother can be hired to breastfeed after her 'iddah ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hiring a mother for breastfeeding after her 'iddah and explain the legal rationale (talil) based on the cessation of the marriage bond.

Core Idea
Once the 'iddah ends, the mother is like a stranger; hiring her is permissible.

This lesson completes the sequence of rulings on hiring a biological mother for breastfeeding. The previous lessons covered the prohibition during marriage and during 'iddah due to the lingering effects of the marriage contract. Now we see that once the 'iddah expires, the marriage bond is entirely severed. The mother becomes like any non-mahram woman (ajnabiyyah), and therefore hiring her for breastfeeding is permissible. The key legal cause (illah) is the complete cessation of the marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring the mother (after 'iddah) to breastfeed her child. The ruling is permissible (jā'iz).
The hukm level is mubah (permissible), not wajib or haram.
2
Identify the condition for permissibility
The condition is that the woman's 'iddah must have expired. If she is still in 'iddah, the prohibition remains.
The 'iddah period is the waiting period after divorce or death.
3
Understand the legal cause (illah)
The illah is that the marriage bond (nikah) has completely ceased (zawāl). This eliminates any obligation of free breastfeeding or any remaining spousal effect.
The text states: "because the marriage has ceased completely."
4
Recognize the legal consequence
As a result, the mother becomes like any other non-mahram woman (ajnabiyyah) whom one may hire for any lawful service, including breastfeeding.
She is no longer considered a wife or mu'taddah.
5
Apply the ruling
Thus, a father may hire his ex-wife after her 'iddah to breastfeed their child, provided a valid hire contract (ijārah) is made with mutual consent and known wage.
This completes the sequence of rulings on hiring the biological mother.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر عورت کی عدت گذر گئی پھر اسے ارضاع کیلئے اجرت پر لیا جائز ہے
و ان انقضت عدتها فاستاجرها یعنی لارضاع ولدها جازلان النكاح قدزال بالكلية وصارت كالاجنبية ترجمہ اور اگر معدہ کی عدت گذرگئی۔ پھر اپنے بچہ کو دودھ پلانے کے واسطے جو اس عورت سے ہے اجارہ پر مقرر کیا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ
And if her 'iddah expires, then he hires her, i.e., to breastfeed her child, it is permissible because the marriage has ceased completely and she has become like a stranger. Translation: And if the mu'taddah's 'iddah has passed, then he hires her to breastfeed their child that is from her, it is permissible because...
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage deals with the case where a divorced woman's 'iddah has ended, and the father wants to hire her to breastfeed their shared child. The ruling is that it is permissible because after the 'iddah, the marriage is completely dissolved with no remaining effects. She is no longer a wife or mu'taddah, so the obligation of free breastfeeding no longer applies. She becomes like any other foreign woman (ajnabiyyah) who can be hired for breastfeeding. Although the text cuts off, the principle is clear: the prohibition only applies while the marriage bond (or its remnants such as 'iddah) exists. Once that is removed, hiring is valid. This completes the sequence of rulings on hiring the biological mother.

Key Terms
أجنبية (ajnabiyyah): A woman who is a stranger (non-mahram) to the man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Never, because it is always wajib on her.

Key Takeaway
After a woman's 'iddah expires, she is treated as a stranger regarding breastfeeding, and hiring her is permissible.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
beginner
8 min
Father's Maintenance Obligation for Minor Child
States ruling with dual proofs and condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a father's obligation to support his minor child and identify the Quranic proof and the condition limiting that obligation.

Core Idea
A father must support his minor child even if the child differs in religion – the child is part of the father.

Family maintenance (nafaqah) is a key obligation in Hanafi fiqh. This lesson examines a specific ruling: the father's duty to provide for his minor child, regardless of religious difference. The text draws on both a direct Quranic command and a powerful analogy to spousal maintenance. We will unpack the evidence and identify the subtle condition that limits the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
Read the opening sentence. The ruling is that nafaqah (maintenance) of a minor child is wajib upon the father, and it applies even if the child's religion differs from the father's. The ruling covers all basic needs like food, clothing, and shelter.
The term 'saghir' (minor) refers to a child who has not reached puberty. This is a key scope condition.
2
Locate the Primary Dalil (Quran)
The text cites Surah al-Baqarah 2:233: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing.' This verse, though addressing mothers, imposes a general obligation on fathers. Identify the operative phrase 'wa 'ala al-mawludi lahu' and note that it is interpreted broadly.
The verse is qati' al-thubut (definitely transmitted) but its indication (dalala) is zanni – it requires interpretation, hence the ruling is wajib, not fard.
3
Analyze the Secondary Proof (Child as Part of Father)
The text adds a rational argument: the child is a part (juz') of the father, so supporting him is like supporting himself. This is a secondary proof reinforcing the obligation.
This argument is used to emphasize that the duty is innate and cannot be negated by religious difference.
4
Understand the Analogy with Wife's Nafaqah
The author draws a parallel: just as a husband must support his wife even if she is non-Muslim, so too must a father support his child. For the wife, the cause (sabab) is the valid marriage contract, which establishes confinement (ihtibas) in exchange for maintenance. The contract is valid between a Muslim and a non-Muslim, so maintenance applies.
The analogy strengthens the ruling for the child case by showing that religious difference does not break maintenance obligations in general.
5
Note the Condition (Child's Own Wealth)
The passage concludes with a condition: the father's obligation only applies if the minor child has no wealth of his own. If the child possesses property, the child's own wealth is used first before the father is required to provide.
This condition is crucial – it prevents double liability and ensures the child's assets are used for their own maintenance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و نفقة الصغير واجبة على ابيه وإن خالفه في دينه كما تجب نفقة الزوجة على الزوج وان خالفته في دينه اما الولد فلاطلاق ماتلونا وعلى الممولودله رزقهن الآية ولانه جزوه فيكون فى معنى نفسه واما الزوجة فلان السبب هو العقد الصحيح فانه بازاء الاحتباس الثابت به وقدصح العقد بين المسلم والكافرة وترتب عليه الاحتباس فوجبت النفقة وفى جميع ماذكرنا انما تجب النفقة على الاب اذالم يكن للصغير مال اذا كان
And the nafaqah of a minor child is obligatory upon the father even if he differs from him in religion, just as the nafaqah of the wife is obligatory upon the husband even if she differs from him in religion. As for the child, due to the absoluteness of what we recited: 'And upon the father is their provision' [Quran 2:233] and because he is a part of him, so he is like himself. As for the wife, because the cause is the valid contract, for it is in exchange for the confinement (ihtibas) established by it. The contract between a Muslim and a disbelieving woman is valid and confinement is established, so nafaqah becomes obligatory. In all that we have mentioned, nafaqah is only obligatory upon the father if the child has no wealth when he is...
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage establishes the general principle that the father is obligated to provide nafaqah (financial support) for his minor child, even if the child is of a different religion than the father (for example, if the child follows the mother's religion or becomes apostate before puberty). The ruling is analogized to the nafaqah of a wife: just as a husband must support his wife even if she is a non-Muslim, so too must a father support his child regardless of religious differences. The proof for the child's nafaqah is the Qur'anic verse 'wa 'ala al-mawludi lahu rizquhunna wa kiswatuhunna bil-ma'ruf' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:233), which commands fathers to provide for their children. Additionally, the child is considered a 'part' (juz') of the father, so supporting the child is like supporting himself. For the wife, the cause (sabab) is the valid marriage contract, which establishes confinement (ihtibas) of the wife in exchange for nafaqah; this applies even if the wife is a non-Muslim because the contract is valid. The passage concludes with a condition: this obligation falls on the father only if the child has no wealth of his own. If the child has property, his own wealth is used first.

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqah): Financial maintenance including food, clothing, and shelter.
صغیر (saghir): A minor child who has not reached puberty.
احتباس (ihtibas): Confinement; the wife's restriction to the husband's home in exchange for nafaqah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is a Muslim father obligated to support his minor child if the child is a non-Muslim?
A) No, because the child is not a Muslim
B) Yes, it is wajib like supporting a non-Muslim wife
C) Only if the child's mother demands it
D) Only if the child has no other relatives

Key Takeaway
A father must provide nafaqah for his minor child regardless of religious difference, with the condition that the child has no personal wealth.

Hiring a Divorced Mother as Wet Nurse
Ruling on permissibility and mother's preferential right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a divorced mother as a wet nurse and apply the principle of preventing harm from the Quran.

Core Idea
A divorced mother after 'iddah is like a stranger, but she is preferred due to compassion.

This lesson examines a nuanced fiqh ruling: a divorced mother, once her 'iddah expires, becomes legally akin to a stranger regarding the contract of wet-nursing. However, Islamic law prioritizes the child's welfare and the mother's unique compassion, granting her a preferential right—provided she does not demand more than the fair market wage. We will explore the proof from the Quran and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the act
The act is hiring a divorced woman (who is the child's mother) as a wet nurse after her 'iddah has ended. Identify the legal status of the woman after 'iddah.
After 'iddah, the marriage is completely dissolved.
2
State the ruling and its basis
The ruling is that this hiring is permissible (jā'iz). The basis is that she is now like any other strange woman (ajnabiyyah), and hiring a stranger is permissible.
Analogy (qiyas) to hiring a stranger.
3
Analyze the mother's right of preference
If the father wants to hire a stranger, but the mother is willing to accept the same wage (ujrat al-mithl) or even less, she is more entitled (aḥaqq) because she is more compassionate and that benefits the child.
The mother's right is conditional on not demanding more than the stranger's wage.
4
Determine the limit on the mother's demand
If the mother demands more than the stranger's wage, the father is not compelled to pay it. This prevents harm (ḍarar) to the father, as indicated by the Quranic verse (2:233).
The verse prohibits harming either parent because of the child.
5
Connect to the Quranic proof
The verse 'Do not harm a mother because of her child, nor a father because of his child' is cited to show that the father cannot be forced to pay above the standard wage, nor can the mother be forced to accept less.
The dalāla (indication) is that imposing extra cost constitutes harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زکاں بالکل زائل ہو گیا اور ( یہ عورت ) اجنبیہ کے مثل ہو گئی ۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ معدہ کی عدت گزر گئی پھر شوہر نے اپنے بچہ کو دودھ پلانے کے واسطے جو اسی عورت سے ہے اس کو اجرت پر مقرر کیا تو یہ اجارہ جائز ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب عدت گذرگئی تو نکاح بالکلیہ زائل ہو گیا اور یہ عورت اجنبیہ کے مانند ہوگئی۔ پس جس طرح اجنبیہ کو اجارہ پر لینا جائز ہے اسی طرح اس کو بھی لینا درست ہو گا۔
اگر باپ بچہ کی ماں کے علاوہ کو اجرت پر لائے اور ماں اجرت مثل پر راضی ہے تو وہ اجنبیہ سے زیادہ مستحق ہے
فان قال الاب لا استاجرها وجاء بغيرها فرضيت الام بمثل اجرالا جنبية اورضيت بغير اجركانت هي احق لانها اشفق فكان نظر اللصبي في الدفع اليها وان التمست زيادة لم يجبر الزوج عليها دفعا للضررعنه واليه لاشارة بقوله تعالى و لا تضار والدة بولدها ولا مولود له بولدهای بالزامه لها اكثر من اجرة الاجنبية
ترجمہ پھر اگر بچہ کے ) باپ نے کہا کہ میں بچہ کی ماں کو اجرت پر نہیں لوں گا ۔ ( بلکہ ) بچہ کی ماں کے علاوہ دوسری دودھ پلانے والی لایا۔ پھر اجنبیہ کی اجرت کے مثل پر (بچہ کی ماں راضی ہوگئی یا بغیر اجرت کے راضی ہوگئی تو یہی مستحق ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ یہ اپنے بچے پر زیادہ شفیق ہے۔ تو اس کو سپرد کرنے میں بچہ کے حق میں زیادہ بہتری ہے اور اگر بچہ کی ماں نے اجنبیہ کی اجرت سے یہ مانا تو شوہر زیادہ دیئے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تا کہ اس سے ضرر دور ہو اور اسی طرف اللہ عزوجل نے ارشاد فرمایا ولا تـضــار والــدة بولدها ولا مولود له بولدہ یعنی ماں اپنے بچہ کی وجہ سے مضرت میں نہ ڈالی جائے گی اور نہ بچہ کا باپ اپنے بچہ کی وجہ سے ضر راٹھا دے گا۔ یعنی اس پر بچہ کی مان کے واسطے اجتہیہ کی اجرت سے زیادہ اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔
تشریح، مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر بچہ کے باپ نے کہا کہ میں اس کی ماں کو اجارہ پر مقر نہیں کروں گا۔ بلکہ اسکے علاوہ دودھ پلانے والی کو لے آیا۔ پھر جس قد را جرت اجتنبیہ مانگتی تھی اسی قدرا جرت پر یا بغیر اجرت کے خود بچے کی ماں راضی ہوگئی تو اس صورت میں بچہ کی ہاں ہی مستحق ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماں اپنے بچہ پر زیادہ شفیق ہے تو اسی کے سپرد کرنے میں بچہ کے حق میں بہتری ہے اور اگر بچہ کی ماں نے اجنبیہ کی اجرت سے زیادہ مانگی تو شوہر یعنی بچہ کے باپ کو زیادہ دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تا کہ اس سے ضر دور ہو اور اسی طرف اللہ رب العزت نے اشارہ فرمایا ولا تضار والدة بولدها ولا مولود له بولده یعنی بچہ کی ماں کیلئے اجتہیہ کی اجرت سے زیادہ مقرر کر کے باپ کو تکلیف نہ پہنچائی جائے بلکہ بچہ اس دودھ پلانے والی انا کے سپرد کر دیا جائے گا۔ وہ اس کی ماں کے پاس رہ کر اس کو پلائے گی۔
And the [marital] ties are completely eradicated, and (this woman) becomes like a stranger. Explanation: The scenario is that the 'iddah of the [former] wife has passed, then the husband hired her to nurse his child, who is from her, for a wage. This hiring is permissible. The proof is that when the 'iddah passed, the marriage completely ceased, and this woman became akin to a stranger. So just as it is permissible to hire a stranger, so too it becomes correct to hire her. If the father brings a wet nurse other than the mother, and the mother is content with the equivalent wage of the stranger, then she is more entitled. For if the father says, 'I will not hire her,' and brings another, and the mother agrees to the equivalent of the stranger's wage or agrees without wage, then she is more entitled because she is more compassionate to her child. So the benefit for the child lies in entrusting [the nursing] to her. And if she demands more, the husband is not compelled to give it, to prevent harm from him. And to this Allah, Exalted and Glorious, has indicated: 'And do not harm a mother because of her child, nor a father because of his child' – meaning the mother will not be harmed because of her child, nor the father because of his child, i.e., he is not obligated to pay more than the wage of a stranger for the mother's sake. Explanation: The issue is that if the child's father said, 'I will not appoint her on hire,' but brought another wet nurse, and the mother then agreed to the same wage as the stranger or agreed without wage, then in this case the child's mother is entitled. The proof is that the mother is more compassionate to her child, so entrusting her is better for the child. And if the mother demands more than the stranger's wage, the husband, i.e., the child's father, is not compelled to pay more, so that harm is removed from him. And Allah, Lord of Honor, has indicated: 'Do not harm a mother because of her child, nor a father because of his child' – meaning that the father should not be burdened by fixing more than the stranger's wage for the mother, but the child should be handed over to this wet nurse; she will stay with the mother and nurse him.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about hiring a divorced woman as a wet nurse after her 'iddah has expired. The author explains that once the 'iddah has passed, the marriage ties are completely severed, and the woman is like a stranger. Therefore, hiring her for nursing is permissible by analogy (qiyas) to hiring a strange woman. The passage then addresses a scenario where the father wants to hire a stranger instead of the child's mother. The ruling states that if the mother is willing to accept the same wage as a stranger (ujrat al-mithl) or even without wage, she is more entitled to nurse her child because of her greater compassion and the child's benefit. However, if the mother demands more than the stranger's wage, the father is not compelled to pay it. This is based on the Quranic verse (2:233) which forbids causing harm to the mother or father because of the child. The commentary clarifies that this ruling applies after the marriage has ended; during the marriage, the mother has a right to nurse her child without compensation. The text follows the Hanafi position that the welfare of the child is paramount, and the mother's right is recognized as long as it does not cause undue harm to the father.

Key Terms
اجنبية (ajnabiyyah): A woman who is not the child's mother and not a mahram; a stranger.
اجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for a wet nurse in that locality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a divorced mother demands more than the standard wage for nursing her child, what is the father's obligation?
A) He must pay her the demanded amount.
B) He is not compelled to pay more than the stranger's wage.
C) He must hire a stranger instead of the mother.
D) He must let the mother nurse without any wage.

Key Takeaway
A divorced mother after 'iddah is entitled to nurse her child for a fair wage; she is preferred due to compassion, but cannot force higher pay.
